inline-share-btn-label-more\">MORE</span></span></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><a href=\"/story/news/local/mesa/2017/02/17/mesa-fire-takes-long-time-supporters-for-a-ride-along/98020090/\">MESA, AZ</a> --\u00a0On Betty Lee\u2019s most recent birthday,\u00a0Mesa Fire and Medical Department Chief Mary Cameli, delivered a photograph to her friend of 20 years.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>During that visit, Lee, 90, told Cameli a story that had inspired her. On a news report the night before, a lady had turned 100 years old, and had always wanted to ride in a police car. The community had rallied together to grant her that wish.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cSo we asked her, in her 90s, what was something she had always wanted to do?\u201d said Cameli. \u201cAnd she said she\u2019s always wanted to get to ride in the firetruck. And so we said, \u2018That\u2019s something we can do.\u2019 \u201d</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div class=\"partner-placement partner-spike\"></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Lee\u2019s late husband, Milt Lee, founded the Mesa Public Safety Foundation in 1976, and Betty worked as the secretary of that group. The foundation helped raise funds, and gave an annual breakfast recognizing first responders and citizens who had helped police or fire personnel in their jobs. Milt passed away in 2012.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cIt was really a PR thing, to get the public and the citizens to know how wonderful our police and fire are,\u201d said\u00a0Lee.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cWhat we did was honor the police and fire each year, those who did heroic deeds, and we had a banquet to present them to the public so the public would be aware of what our police and fire department were doing,\u201d said\u00a0Wayne Pomeroy.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Pomeroy, 94, is a lifelong resident of Mesa\u00a0and took over the Public Safety Foundation after two terms as mayor, ending in 1980. During his time in office, Pomeroy said, he helped implement the 911 system, and the paramedic program of the Mesa fire department.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>And so, on a sunny afternoon Thursday, a nearly 34-foot firetruck rolled into a quiet neighborhood near the Mesa Country Club, and stopped at the end of a cul-de-sac in front of Pomeroy\u2019s home.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Firefighters\u00a0Jake Bennett, Sean Couden, engineer Dan Hammerl and Capt.\u00a0Casey Russell helped the two nonagenarians down the driveway, and carefully lifted them into the truck. Mesa Councilman\u00a0Mark Freeman\u00a0and Pomeroy's daughter Michelle Pomeroy came along for the once-in-a-lifetime ride.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>After securing the\u00a0precious cargo, the crew of Mesa Fire Engine 201 fired up the lights, and took off for a twirl around the neighborhood.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cI\u2019m glad that I was invited to come, because I really only did the secretarial part of it. It\u2019s my husband that they\u2019re really honoring,\u201d said\u00a0Lee.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\u201cThey\u2019ve been supportive of us for many, many years, and this was just a small way that we can give back and say thank you for the many, many years of service that you have provided for public safety,\u201d said Cameli.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>***</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>For more stories like this, <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/humankindvideos/\">LIKE Humankind on "http://rssfeeds.usatoday.com/~/277242438/0/usatoday-newstopstories~For-her-th-birthday-this-woman-got-a-special-gift/", "date": "03-04-2017", "source": "new-york-times", "text": "CLOSE Skip in Skip x Embed x Share When Betty had her 90th birthday, she did something she always wanted to do. HUMANKIND\n\nBetty Lee, 90, gets a kiss on the cheek from Mesa Fire and Medical Department Chief Mary Cameli. (Photo: Hannah Gaber/The Arizona Republic)\n\nMESA, AZ -- On Betty Lee\u2019s most recent birthday, Mesa Fire and Medical Department Chief Mary Cameli, delivered a photograph to her friend of 20 years.\n\nDuring that visit, Lee, 90, told Cameli a story that had inspired her. On a news report the night before, a lady had turned 100 years old, and had always wanted to ride in a police car. The community had rallied together to grant her that wish.\n\n\u201cSo we asked her, in her 90s, what was something she had always wanted to do?\u201d said Cameli. \u201cAnd she said she\u2019s always wanted to get to ride in the firetruck. And so we said, \u2018That\u2019s something we can do.\u2019 \u201d\n\nLee\u2019s late husband, Milt Lee, founded the Mesa Public Safety Foundation in 1976, and Betty worked as the secretary of that group. The foundation helped raise funds, and gave an annual breakfast recognizing first responders and citizens who had helped police or fire personnel in their jobs. Milt passed away in 2012.\n\n\u201cIt was really a PR thing, to get the public and the citizens to know how wonderful our police and fire are,\u201d said Lee.\n\n\u201cWhat we did was honor the police and fire each year, those who did heroic deeds, and we had a banquet to present them to the public so the public would be aware of what our police and fire department were doing,\u201d said Wayne Pomeroy.\n\nPomeroy, 94, is a lifelong resident of Mesa and took over the Public Safety Foundation after two terms as mayor, ending in 1980. During his time in office, Pomeroy said, he helped implement the 911 system, and the paramedic program of the Mesa fire department.\n\nAnd so, on a sunny afternoon Thursday, a nearly 34-foot firetruck rolled into a quiet neighborhood near the Mesa Country Club, and stopped at the end of a cul-de-sac in front of Pomeroy\u2019s home.\n\nFirefighters Jake Bennett, Sean Couden, engineer Dan Hammerl and Capt. Casey Russell helped the two nonagenarians down the driveway, and carefully lifted them into the truck. Mesa Councilman Mark Freeman and Pomeroy's daughter Michelle Pomeroy came along for the once-in-a-lifetime ride.\n\nAfter securing the precious cargo, the crew of Mesa Fire Engine 201 fired up the lights, and took off for a twirl around the neighborhood.\n\n\u201cI\u2019m glad that I was invited to come, because I really only did the secretarial part of it. It\u2019s my husband that they\u2019re really honoring,\u201d said Lee.\n\n\u201cThey\u2019ve been supportive of us for many, many years, and this was just a small way that we can give back and say thank you for the many, many years of service that you have provided for public safety,\u201d said Cameli.\n\n***\n\nFor more stories like this, LIKE Humankind on Facebook.\n\nCLOSE Skip in Skip x Embed x Share HUMANKIND: STORIES WORTH SHARING Baby moonwalks to Michael Jackson's 'Beat It' | 1:04 What happens when you combine an exhausted stay-at-home dad, a four-month-old baby and some smooth dance moves?
